href="#cite_note-GDP2011-6">[6]</a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row">&#160;&#8226;&#160;Per capita</th><td>C$65,556 (<a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories_by_gross_domestic_product" title="List of Canadian provinces and territories by gross domestic product">5th</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Time_in_Canada" title="Time in Canada">Time zone</a></th><td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC" title="UTC">UTC</a>&#8722;3.5 for Newfoundland<br/>UTC&#8722;4 for Labrador (Black Tickle and North)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_subnational_postal_abbreviations" title="Canadian subnational postal abbreviations">Postal abbr.</a></th><td class="adr"><div class="postal-code">NL (formerly NF)</div></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_postal_code" title="Canadian postal code">Postal code prefix</a></th><td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_A_Postal_Codes_of_Canada" title="List of A Postal Codes of Canada">A</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td class="nickname"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:CA" title="ISO 3166-2:CA">CA-NL</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Flower</th><td><a href="/wiki/Sarracenia_purpurea" title="Sarracenia purpurea">Pitcher plant</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row">Tree</th><td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_spruce" title="Black spruce">Black spruce</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row">Bird</th><td><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_puffin" title="Atlantic puffin">Atlantic puffin</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td><span class="url"><a class="external text" href="http://www.gov.nl.ca" rel="nofollow">www<wbr/>.gov<wbr/>.nl<wbr/>.ca</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left; font-size:smaller">Rankings include all <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">provinces and territories</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Newfoundland and Labrador</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#716;/: secondary stress follows">&#716;</span><span title="/nj/: \'n\' in \'new\'">nj</span><span title="/u&#720;/: \'oo\' in \'goose\'">u&#720;</span><span title="\'f\' in \'find\'">f</span><span title="/&#601;n/: \'on\' in \'button\'">&#601;n</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span></span>&#8201;...&#8201;<wbr/><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">b</span><span title="\'r\' in \'rye\'">r</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span><span title="/&#596;&#720;r/: \'ar\' in \'war\'">&#596;&#720;r</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Terre-Neuve-et-Labrador</i>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montagnais_language" title="Montagnais language">Montagnais</a>: <i lang="moe">Akamassiss</i>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newfoundland_Irish" title="Newfoundland Irish">Newfoundland Irish</a>: <i lang="ga-CA" title="Irish language text">Talamh an &#201;isc agus Labradar</i>) is the most easterly <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. Situated in the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic region</a>, it comprises the island of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a> and mainland <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">Labrador</a> to the northwest, with a combined area of 405,212 square kilometres (156,500&#160;sq&#160;mi). In 2013, the province\'s population was estimated at 526,702.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stats_Canada_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stats_Canada-7">[7]</a></sup> About 92% of the province\'s population lives on the island of Newfoundland (and its neighbouring smaller islands), of whom more than half live on the <a href="/wiki/Avalon_Peninsula" title="Avalon Peninsula">Avalon Peninsula</a>.\n</p><p>The province is Canada\'s most linguistically <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homogeneous" title="Homogeneous">homogeneous</a>, with 97.6% of residents reporting English (<a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_English" title="Newfoundland English">Newfoundland English</a>) as their mother tongue in the 2006 census.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Historically, Newfoundland was also home to unique varieties of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_French" title="Newfoundland French">French</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newfoundland_Irish" title="Newfoundland Irish">Irish</a>, as well as the extinct <a href="/wiki/Beothuk_language" title="Beothuk language">Beothuk language</a>. In Labrador, the indigenous languages <a href="/wiki/Innu_language" title="Innu language">Innu-aimun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inuktitut" title="Inuktitut">Inuktitut</a> are also spoken.\n</p><p>Newfoundland and Labrador\'s capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="St. John\'s, Newfoundland and Labrador">St. John\'s</a>, is Canada\'s 20th-largest <a href="/wiki/Census_geographic_units_of_Canada" title="Census geographic units of Canada">census metropolitan area</a> and is home to almost 40 percent of the province\'s population. St. John\'s is the seat of government, home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="House of Assembly of Newfoundland and Labrador">House of Assembly of Newfoundland and Labrador</a> and to the highest court in the jurisdiction, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador_Court_of_Appeal" title="Newfoundland and Labrador Court of Appeal">Newfoundland and Labrador Court of Appeal</a>.\n</p><p>A former <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_Colony" title="Newfoundland Colony">colony</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">dominion</a> of the United Kingdom, Newfoundland gave up its independence in 1933, following significant economic distress caused by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> and the aftermath of Newfoundland\'s participation in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. It became the tenth province to enter the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">Canadian Confederation</a> on March 31, 1949, as "Newfoundland". On December 6, 2001, an <a href="/wiki/Amendments_to_the_Constitution_of_Canada" title="Amendments to the Constitution of Canada">amendment</a> was made to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Canada" title="Constitution of Canada">Constitution of Canada</a> to <a href="/wiki/Geographical_renaming" title="Geographical renaming">change the province\'s official name</a> to Newfoundland and Labrador.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r872693506">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Etymology"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Etymology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Geography"><span class="toctext">Government and politics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Art"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Art</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Literature"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span class="toctext">Literature</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Prose_fiction"><span class="tocnumber">9.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Prose fiction</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-21"><a href="#Poetry"><span class="tocnumber">9.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Poetry</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22"><a href="#Playwrights"><span class="tocnumber">9.4</span> <span class="toctext">Languages spoken in the Province</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Sports"><span symbols</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name "Newfoundland" is a translation of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> <i lang="pt" title="Portuguese language text">Terra Nova</i>, which literally means "new land" and is also reflected in the French name for the Province\'s island part (<i lang="fr" title="French language text">Terre-Neuve</i>). The influence of early Portuguese exploration is also reflected in the name of Labrador, which derives from the surname of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1415%E2%80%931578)#Chronology_of_the_Portuguese_discoveries" title="History of Portugal (1415&#8211;1578)">Portuguese navigator</a> <span lang="pt" style="font-style:normal;" title="Portuguese language text"><a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Fernandes_Lavrador" title="Jo&#227;o Fernandes Lavrador">Jo&#227;o Fernandes Lavrador</a></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Labrador\'s name in the <a href="/wiki/Inuttitut" title="Inuttitut">Inuttitut</a> language (spoken in <a href="/wiki/Nunatsiavut" title="Nunatsiavut">Nunatsiavut</a>) is <i lang="iu" title="Inuktitut language text">Nunatsuak</i>, meaning "the big land" (a common English nickname for Labrador). Newfoundland\'s Inuttitut name is <i lang="iu" title="Inuktitut language text">Ikkarumikluak</i> meaning "place of many shoals".\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Geography of Newfoundland and Labrador">Geography of Newfoundland and Labrador</a></div>\n<p>Newfoundland and Labrador is the most easterly province in Canada, and is located at the north-eastern corner of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geo_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Geo-11">[11]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Belle_Isle" title="Strait of Belle Isle">Strait of Belle Isle</a> separates the province into two geographical divisions: Labrador, which is a large area of mainland Canada, and Newfoundland, an island in the Atlantic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sve_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-sve-12">[12]</a></sup> The province also includes over 7,000 tiny islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlas_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-atlas-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Newfoundland is roughly triangular. Each side is about 400&#160;km (250&#160;mi) long, and its area is 108,860&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (42,030&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlas_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-atlas-13">[13]</a></sup> Newfoundland and its neighbouring small islands (excluding French possessions) have a total area of 111,390&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (43,010&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NF_gov_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-NF_gov-14">[14]</a></sup> Newfoundland extends between latitudes 46&#176;36&#8242;N and 51&#176;38&#8242;N.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-abc-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cde_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-cde-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Labrador is an irregular shape: the western part of its border with <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Drainage_divide" title="Drainage divide">drainage divide</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Labrador_Peninsula" title="Labrador Peninsula">Labrador Peninsula</a>. Lands drained by rivers that flow into the Atlantic Ocean are part of Labrador, and the rest belongs to Quebec. Most of Labrador\'s southern boundary with Quebec follows the 52nd parallel of latitude. Labrador\'s extreme northern tip, at 60&#176;22&#8242;N, shares a short border with <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a>. Labrador\'s area (including associated small islands) is 294,330&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (113,640&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NF_gov_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-NF_gov-14">[14]</a></sup> Together, Newfoundland and Labrador make up 4.06% of Canada\'s area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlas_area_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-atlas_area-17">[17]</a></sup> with a total area of 405,720&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (156,650&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NLW_GrosMorne1_tango7174.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1440" decoding="async" height="92" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/NLW_GrosMorne1_tango7174.jpg/220px-NLW_GrosMorne1_tango7174.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/NLW_GrosMorne1_tango7174.jpg/330px-NLW_GrosMorne1_tango7174.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/NLW_GrosMorne1_tango7174.jpg/440px-NLW_GrosMorne1_tango7174.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NLW_GrosMorne1_tango7174.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Long_Range_Mountains" title="Long Range Mountains">Long Range Mountains</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Labrador is the easternmost part of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Shield" title="Canadian Shield">Canadian Shield</a>, a vast area of ancient <a href="/wiki/Metamorphic_rock" title="Metamorphic rock">metamorphic rock</a> comprising much of northeastern <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>. Colliding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plate_tectonic" title="Plate tectonic">tectonic</a> plates have shaped much of the geology of Newfoundland. <a href="/wiki/Gros_Morne_National_Park" title="Gros Morne National Park">Gros Morne National Park</a> has a reputation as an outstanding example of tectonics at work,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-just_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-just-19">[19]</a></sup> and as such has been designated a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Long_Range_Mountains" title="Long Range Mountains">Long Range Mountains</a> on Newfoundland\'s west coast are the northeasternmost extension of the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sve_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-sve-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Churchillfalls08.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3888" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Churchillfalls08.JPG/220px-Churchillfalls08.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Churchillfalls08.JPG/330px-Churchillfalls08.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Churchillfalls08.JPG/440px-Churchillfalls08.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Churchillfalls08.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Churchill_Falls" title="Churchill Falls">Churchill Falls</a> in Labrador</div></div></div>\n<p>The north-south extent of the province (46&#176;36&#8242;N to 60&#176;22&#8242;N), prevalent westerly winds, cold ocean currents and local factors such as mountains and coastline combine to create the various climates of the province.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tre_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-tre-20">[20]</a></sup> Northern Labrador is classified as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polar_region" title="Polar region">polar</a> <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> climate, southern Labrador has a <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a>, while most of Newfoundland has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (Dfb under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification_system" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification system">K&#246;ppen climate classification system</a>): cool summer subtype.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newfoundland_and_Labrador_K%C3%B6ppen.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="810" decoding="async" height="391" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Newfoundland_and_Labrador_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/220px-Newfoundland_and_Labrador_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Newfoundland_and_Labrador_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/330px-Newfoundland_and_Labrador_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Newfoundland_and_Labrador_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/440px-Newfoundland_and_Labrador_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newfoundland_and_Labrador_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen climate types</a> of Newfoundland and Labrador. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subpolar_oceanic" title="Subpolar oceanic">subpolar oceanic</a> (Cfc) region is a tiny strip on the southeast coast.</div></div></div>\n<p>Newfoundland and Labrador has a wide range of climates and weather,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-at_home_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-at_home-21">[21]</a></sup> due to its geography. The island of Newfoundland spans 5 degrees of latitude, comparable to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-at_home_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-at_home-21">[21]</a></sup>\nThe province has been divided into six climate types, but broadly Newfoundland has a cool summer subtype of a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a>, which is greatly influenced by the sea since no part of the island is more than 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) from the ocean. Northern Labrador is classified as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polar_region" title="Polar region">polar</a> <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a> climate, southern Labrador has a <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ses_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-ses-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Monthly average temperatures, rainfall and snowfall for four places are shown in the attached graphs. <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="St. John\'s, Newfoundland and Labrador">St. John\'s</a> represents the east coast, <a href="/wiki/Gander,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Gander, Newfoundland and Labrador">Gander</a> the interior of the island, <a href="/wiki/Corner_Brook" title="Corner Brook">Corner Brook</a> the west coast of the island and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wabush,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Wabush, Newfoundland and Labrador">Wabush</a> the interior of Labrador. Climate data for 56 places in the province is available from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environment_Canada" title="Environment Canada">Environment Canada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The data for the graphs is the average over thirty years. Error bars on the temperature graph indicate the range of daytime highs and night time lows. Snowfall is the total amount that fell during the month, not the amount accumulated on the ground. This distinction is particularly important for St. John\'s, where a heavy snowfall can be followed by rain, so that no snow remains on the ground.\n</p><p>Surface water temperatures on the Atlantic side reach a summer average of 12&#160;&#176;C (54&#160;&#176;F) inshore and 9&#160;&#176;C (48&#160;&#176;F) offshore to winter lows of &#8722;1&#160;&#176;C (30&#160;&#176;F) inshore and 2&#160;&#176;C (36&#160;&#176;F) offshore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ghi_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-ghi-24">[24]</a></sup> Sea temperatures on the west coast are warmer than Atlantic side by 1 to 3&#160;&#176;C (1 to 5&#160;&#176;F). The sea keeps winter temperatures slightly higher and summer temperatures a little lower on the coast than inland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ghi_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-ghi-24">[24]</a></sup> The maritime climate produces more variable weather, ample precipitation in a variety of forms, greater <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">humidity</a>, lower visibility, more clouds, less sunshine, and higher winds than a continental climate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ghi_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-ghi-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin:auto;">\n<caption>Average daily maximum and minimum temperatures for selected locations in Newfoundland and Labrador<sup class="reference" Newfoundland and Labrador">Nain</a></td>\n<td>15/5</td>\n<td>59/41</td>\n<td>&#8722;14/&#8722;23</td>\n<td>7/&#8722;10\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="margin:auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><div
