snowfall<i></i></div></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="History of Newfoundland and Labrador">History of Newfoundland and Labrador</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonisation">Pre-colonisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Pre-colonisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carlb-beothuk-museum-2002.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="559" data-file-width="594" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Carlb-beothuk-museum-2002.jpg/220px-Carlb-beothuk-museum-2002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Carlb-beothuk-museum-2002.jpg/330px-Carlb-beothuk-museum-2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Carlb-beothuk-museum-2002.jpg/440px-Carlb-beothuk-museum-2002.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carlb-beothuk-museum-2002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Beothuk" title="Beothuk">Beothuk</a> tribe of Newfoundland is extinct but represented in museum, historical and archeological records.</div></div></div>\n<p>Human habitation in Newfoundland and Labrador can be traced back about 9,000 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>  The <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Archaic" title="Maritime Archaic">Maritime Archaic peoples</a> were groups of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaic_stage" title="Archaic stage">Archaic</a> cultures of sea-mammal hunters in the <a href="/wiki/Subarctic" title="Subarctic">subarctic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bogucki_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bogucki-27">[27]</a></sup> They prospered along the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Atlantic Coast</a> of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> from about 7000&#160;BC to 1500&#160;BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Their settlements included <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Longhouses" title="Longhouses">longhouses</a> and boat-topped temporary or seasonal houses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bogucki_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bogucki-27">[27]</a></sup> They engaged in long-distance trade, using as currency white <a href="/wiki/Chert" title="Chert">chert</a>, a rock quarried from northern Labrador to <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The southern branch of these people was established on the north peninsula of Newfoundland by 5,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pastore_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-pastore-30">[30]</a></sup> The Maritime Archaic period is best known from a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mortuary" title="Mortuary">mortuary</a> site in Newfoundland at <a href="/wiki/Port_au_Choix" title="Port au Choix">Port au Choix</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bogucki_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bogucki-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Maritime Archaic peoples were gradually displaced by people of the <a href="/wiki/Dorset_culture" title="Dorset culture">Dorset culture</a> (Late <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Eskimo" title="Paleo-Eskimo">Paleo-Eskimo</a>) who also occupied Port au Choix. The number of their sites discovered on Newfoundland indicates they may have been the most numerous group of Aboriginal people to live there. They thrived from about 2000 BC to AD 800. Many of their sites were located on exposed headlands and outer islands. They were more oriented to the sea than earlier peoples, and had developed sleds and boats similar to kayaks. They burned seal blubber in soapstone lamps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pastore_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-pastore-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>Many of these sites, such as <a href="/wiki/Port_au_Choix" title="Port au Choix">Port au Choix</a>, recently excavated by Memorial archaeologist, Priscilla Renouf, are quite large and show evidence of a long-term commitment to place. Renouf has excavated huge amounts of <a href="/wiki/Harp_seal" title="Harp seal">harp seal</a> bones at Port au Choix, indicating that this place was a prime location for the hunting of these animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pastore_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-pastore-30">[30]</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>The people of the Dorset Culture (800 BC &#8211; AD 1500) were highly adapted to living in a very cold climate, and much of their food came from hunting sea mammals through holes in the ice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wonders_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wonders-31">[31]</a></sup> The massive decline in sea ice during the <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Warm_Period" title="Medieval Warm Period">Medieval Warm Period</a> would have had a devastating impact upon their way of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wonders_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wonders-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The appearance of the Beothuk culture is believed to be the most recent cultural manifestation of peoples who first migrated from Labrador to Newfoundland around 1 AD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-32">[32]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a>, found mostly in Labrador, are the descendants of what <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropologists</a> call the <a href="/wiki/Thule_people" title="Thule people">Thule people</a>, who emerged from western Alaska around AD 1000 and spread eastwards across the High Arctic, reaching Labrador around 1300&#8211;1500.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Researchers believe that the Dorset culture lacked the dogs, larger weapons and other technologies that gave the expanding Inuit people an advantage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Over time, groups started to focus on resources available to them locally.\n</p><p>The inhabitants eventually organized themselves into small <a href="/wiki/Band_society" title="Band society">bands</a> of a few families, grouped into larger <a href="/wiki/Tribe" title="Tribe">tribes</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chieftainship" title="Chieftainship">chieftainships</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Innu" title="Innu">Innu</a> are the inhabitants of an area they refer to as <i><a href="/wiki/Nitassinan" title="Nitassinan">Nitassinan</a></i>, i.e. most of what is now referred to as northeastern <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> and Labrador. Their subsistence activities were historically centred on hunting and trapping <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribou" title="Caribou">caribou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a> and small game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Luebering_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Luebering-35">[35]</a></sup> Coastal clans also practiced agriculture, fished and managed <a href="/wiki/Maple_sugar" title="Maple sugar">maple sugar</a> bush.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Luebering_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-Luebering-35">[35]</a></sup> The Innu engaged in tribal warfare along the coast of Labrador with the Inuit groups that had significant populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mi%27kmaq_people" title="Mi\'kmaq people">The Mi\'kmaq</a> of southern Newfoundland spent most of their time on the shores harvesting seafood; during the winter they would move inland to the woods to hunt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Over time, the Mi\'kmaq and Innu divided their lands into traditional "districts". Each district was independently governed and had a district chief and a council. The council members were band chiefs, elders and other worthy community leaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-William_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-William-38">[38]</a></sup> In addition to the district councils, the Mi\'kmaq tribes also had (have) a Grand Council or <i>Sant&#233; Mawi&#243;mi</i>, which according to oral tradition was formed before 1600.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Descendants_of_the_Beothuks">Descendants of the Beothuks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Descendants of the Beothuks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<table class="box-Refimprove_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Newfoundland+and+Labrador%22" rel="nofollow">"Newfoundland and Labrador"</a>&#160;&#8211;&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Newfoundland+and+Labrador%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">news</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Newfoundland+and+Labrador%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Newfoundland+and+Labrador%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Newfoundland+and+Labrador%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Newfoundland+and+Labrador%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>By the time that European contact with Newfoundland began in the early 16th century, the Beothuk were the only indigenous group living permanently on the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-32">[32]</a></sup> Unlike other groups in the Northeastern area of the Americas, the Beothuk never established sustained trading relations with European settlers. Instead, their trading interactions were sporadic, and they largely attempted to avoid contact in order to preserve their culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beothuk_Eve_of_Extinction_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beothuk_Eve_of_Extinction-40">[40]</a></sup> The establishment of English fishing operations on the outer coastline of the island, and their later expansion into bays and inlets, cut off access for the Beothuk to their traditional sources of food.\n</p><p>In the 18th century, as the Beothuk were driven further inland by these encroachments, violence between Beothuk and settlers escalated, with each retaliating against the other in their competition for resources. By the early 19th century, violence, starvation, and exposure to tuberculosis had decimated the Beothuk population, and they were extinct as a cultural group by 1829.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Geneticists have suggested that some Icelanders may carry Beothuk DNA, which has been passed down matrilineally over the centuries. This suggests that when the Vikings abandoned their colonization of Newfoundland around 1000 AD, they might have brought back <a href="/wiki/Beothuk" title="Beothuk">Beothuk</a> women to <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_contact">European contact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: European contact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:L%27Anse_aux_Meadows,_recreated_long_house.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2160" data-file-width="3840" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows%2C_recreated_long_house.jpg/220px-L%27Anse_aux_Meadows%2C_recreated_long_house.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows%2C_recreated_long_house.jpg/330px-L%27Anse_aux_Meadows%2C_recreated_long_house.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows%2C_recreated_long_house.jpg/440px-L%27Anse_aux_Meadows%2C_recreated_long_house.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:L%27Anse_aux_Meadows,_recreated_long_house.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows" title="L\'Anse aux Meadows">L\'Anse aux Meadows</a> on Newfoundland, site of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viking" title="Viking">Norse</a> colony</div></div></div>\n<p>The oldest confirmed accounts of European contact date from a thousand years ago as described in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viking" title="Viking">Viking</a> (Norse) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Icelandic_Sagas" title="Icelandic Sagas">Icelandic Sagas</a>. Around the year 1001, the sagas refer to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leif_Ericson" title="Leif Ericson">Leif Ericson</a> landing in three places to the west,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-P&#225;lsson_1965_28_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-P&#225;lsson_1965_28-42">[42]</a></sup> the first two being <a href="/wiki/Helluland" title="Helluland">Helluland</a> (possibly <a href="/wiki/Baffin_Island" title="Baffin Island">Baffin Island</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Markland" title="Markland">Markland</a> (possibly <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">Labrador</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vikings:_The_North_Atlantic_Saga_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vikings:_The_North_Atlantic_Saga-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Leif\'s third landing was at a place he called <a href="/wiki/Vinland" title="Vinland">Vinland</a> (possibly Newfoundland).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Archaeological evidence of a Norse settlement was found in <a href="/wiki/L%27Anse_aux_Meadows" title="L\'Anse aux Meadows">L\'Anse aux Meadows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>, which was declared a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_site" title="World Heritage site">World Heritage site</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> in 1978.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are several other unconfirmed accounts of European discovery and exploration, one tale by men from the Channel Islands being blown off course in the late 15th century into a strange land full of fish, and another from Portuguese maps that depict the <a href="/wiki/Bacalao" title="Bacalao">Terra do Bacalhau</a>, or land of codfish, west of the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>. The earliest, though, is the <a href="/wiki/Brendan" title="Brendan">Voyage of Saint Brendan</a>, the fantastical account of an Irish monk who made a sea voyage in the early 6th century. While the story itself became a part of myth and legend, some historians believe it is based on fact.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>In 1496 <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">John Cabot</a> obtained a charter from English King <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII</a> to "sail to all parts, countries and seas of the East, the West and of the North, under our banner and ensign and to set up our banner on any new-found-land" and on June 24, 1497, landed in <a href="/wiki/Cape_Bonavista" title="Cape Bonavista">Cape Bonavista</a>. Historians disagree on whether Cabot landed in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> in 1497 or in Newfoundland, or possibly Maine, if he landed at all, but Bonavista is recognised by the governments of Canada and the United Kingdom as being Cabot\'s "official" landing place. In 1499 and 1500, Portuguese mariners <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Fernandes_Lavrador" title="Jo&#227;o Fernandes Lavrador">Jo&#227;o Fernandes Lavrador</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P%C3%AAro_de_Barcelos" title="P&#234;ro de Barcelos">P&#234;ro de Barcelos</a> explored and mapped the coast, the former\'s name appearing as "Labrador" on topographical maps of the period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Based on the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Portuguese_monarchs" title="List of Portuguese monarchs">Portuguese Crown</a> claimed it had territorial rights in the area visited by <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">John Cabot</a> in 1497 and 1498.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>  Subsequently, in 1501 and 1502 the <a href="/wiki/Corte-Real_family" title="Corte-Real family">Corte-Real brothers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Corte-Real" title="Miguel Corte-Real">Miguel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Corte-Real" title="Gaspar Corte-Real">Gaspar</a>, explored Newfoundland and Labrador, claiming them as part of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joao_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-joao-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bailey_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bailey-52">[52]</a></sup> In 1506, king <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">Manuel I of Portugal</a> created taxes for the cod fisheries in Newfoundland waters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_%C3%81lvares_Fagundes" title="Jo&#227;o &#193;lvares Fagundes">Jo&#227;o &#193;lvares Fagundes</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P%C3%AAro_de_Barcelos" title="P&#234;ro de Barcelos">P&#234;ro de Barcelos</a> established seasonal fishing outposts in Newfoundland and Nova Scotia around 1521, and older Portuguese settlements may have existed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>  Sir <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Gilbert" title="Humphrey Gilbert">Humphrey Gilbert</a>, provided with <a href="/wiki/Letters_patent" title="Letters patent">letters patent</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_I" title="Queen Elizabeth I">Queen Elizabeth I</a>, landed in St John\'s in August 1583, and formally took possession of the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colony_of_Newfoundland"><span id="colony"></span>Colony of Newfoundland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Colony of Newfoundland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_Colony" title="Newfoundland Colony">Newfoundland Colony</a></div>\n<p>Sometime before 1563 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basque_people" title="Basque people">Basque</a> fishermen, who had been fishing <a href="/wiki/Cod" title="Cod">cod</a> shoals off Newfoundland\'s coasts since the beginning of the sixteenth century, founded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plaisance,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Plaisance, Newfoundland and Labrador">Plaisance</a> (today Placentia), a seasonal haven which French fishermen later also used. In the Newfoundland will, now in an archive in Spain, of the Basque seaman Domingo de Luca dated 1563 de Luca asks "that my body be buried in this port of Plazen&#231;ia in the place where those who die here are usually buried".  This will is the oldest known civil document written in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Twenty years later in 1583 Newfoundland became England\'s first possession in North America and one of the earliest permanent English colonies in the New World<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (November 2016)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup> when <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Gilbert" title="Humphrey Gilbert">Sir Humphrey Gilbert</a> claimed it for <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Queen Elizabeth</a>. Though English fishing boats had visited Newfoundland continuously since Cabot\'s second voyage in 1498 and seasonal fishing camps had existed for a century prior, the Basque, French, and Portuguese had done likewise. In 1585, however, this changed: <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Drake" title="Bernard Drake">Bernard Drake</a> led a <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_expedition_(1585)" title="Newfoundland expedition (1585)">devastating raid</a> on the Spanish and Portuguese fisheries from which they never recovered. This provided an opportunity to secure the island and led to the appointment of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proprietary_Governor" title="Proprietary Governor">Proprietary Governors</a> to establish colonial settlements on the island from 1610 to 1728. <a href="/wiki/John_Guy_(governor)" title="John Guy (governor)">John Guy</a> became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador_lieutenant-governors" title="List of Newfoundland and Labrador lieutenant-governors">governor</a> of the first settlement at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuper%27s_Cove,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Cuper\'s Cove, Newfoundland and Labrador">Cuper\'s Cove</a>. Other settlements included <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subdivision_1I,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador#Bristol\'s_Hope" title="Subdivision 1I, Newfoundland and Labrador">Bristol\'s Hope</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renews" title="Renews">Renews</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Cambriol" title="New Cambriol">New Cambriol</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Falkland" title="South Falkland">South Falkland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Avalon" title="Province of Avalon">Avalon</a> (which became a province in 1623). The first governor given jurisdiction over all of Newfoundland was <a href="/wiki/David_Kirke" title="David Kirke">Sir David Kirke</a> in 1638.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mikak_and_Tukauk.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="576" data-file-width="505" decoding="async" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Mikak_and_Tukauk.jpg/220px-Mikak_and_Tukauk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Mikak_and_Tukauk.jpg/330px-Mikak_and_Tukauk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Mikak_and_Tukauk.jpg/440px-Mikak_and_Tukauk.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mikak_and_Tukauk.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A painting of the <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> woman <a href="/wiki/Mikak" title="Mikak">Mikak</a> and her son, by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Russell_(painter)" title="John Russell (painter)">John Russell</a> in 1769.</div></div></div>\n<p>Explorers quickly realized that the waters around Newfoundland had the best fishing in the North Atlantic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (November 2016)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup> By 1620, 300 fishing boats worked the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Banks_of_Newfoundland" title="Grand Banks of Newfoundland">Grand Banks</a>, employing some 10,000 sailors; many continuing to come from the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country</a>, Normandy, or Brittany. They dried and salted cod on the coast and sold it to Spain and Portugal. Heavy investment by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Calvert" title="George Calvert">Sir George Calvert</a>, 1st Baron Baltimore, in the 1620s in wharves, warehouses, and fishing stations failed to pay off. French raids hurt the business, and the weather was terrible, so he redirected his attention to his <a href="/wiki/History_of_Maryland" title="History of Maryland">other colony in Maryland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> After Calvert left, small-scale entrepreneurs such as Sir David Kirke made good use of the facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>  Kirke became the first governor of Newfoundland in 1638. A <a href="/wiki/Triangular_trade" title="Triangular trade">triangular trade</a> with New England, the West Indies, and Europe gave Newfoundland an important economic role.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> By the 1670s there were 1,700 permanent residents and another 4,500 in the summer months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1655 France appointed a governor in Plaisance, the formerly Basque fishing settlement, thus starting a formal French colonization period in Newfoundland<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> as well as a period of periodic war and unrest between England and France in the region. The Mi\'kmaq, as allies of the French, were amenable to limited French settlement in their midst and fought alongside them against the English. English attacks on Placentia provoked retaliation by <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> explorer <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Le_Moyne_d%27Iberville" title="Pierre Le Moyne d\'Iberville">Pierre Le Moyne d\'Iberville</a> who during <a href="/wiki/King_William%27s_War" title="King William\'s War">King William\'s War</a> in the 1690s destroyed nearly every English settlement on the island. The entire population of the English colony was either killed, captured for ransom, or sentenced to expulsion to England, with the exception of those who withstood the attack at <a href="/wiki/Carbonear_Island" title="Carbonear Island">Carbonear Island</a> and those in the then remote <a href="/wiki/Bonavista,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Bonavista, Newfoundland and Labrador">Bonavista</a>. After France lost political control of the area after the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Port_Royal_(1710)" title="Siege of Port Royal (1710)">Siege of Port Royal in 1710</a>, the M&#237;\'kmaq engaged in warfare with the British throughout <a href="/wiki/Dummer%27s_War" title="Dummer\'s War">Dummer\'s War</a> (1722&#8211;1725), <a href="/wiki/King_George%27s_War" title="King George\'s War">King George\'s War</a> (1744&#8211;1748), <a href="/wiki/Father_Le_Loutre%27s_War" title="Father Le Loutre\'s War">Father Le Loutre\'s War</a> (1749&#8211;1755) and the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a> (1754&#8211;1763). The French colonization period lasted until the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> of 1713, which ended the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>: France ceded to the British its claims to Newfoundland (including its claims to the shores of <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">Hudson Bay</a>) and to the French possessions in <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a>. Afterward, under the supervision of the last French governor, the French population of Plaisance moved to &#206;le Royale (now <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a>), part of Acadia which remained then under French control.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cooks_Karte_von_Neufundland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1462" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Cooks_Karte_von_Neufundland.jpg/220px-Cooks_Karte_von_Neufundland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Cooks_Karte_von_Neufundland.jpg/330px-Cooks_Karte_von_Neufundland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Cooks_Karte_von_Neufundland.jpg/440px-Cooks_Karte_von_Neufundland.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cooks_Karte_von_Neufundland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 1775 map published by <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> of Newfoundland and parts of Labrador</div></div></div>\n<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> (1713), France had acknowledged British ownership of the island. However, in the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years\' War">Seven Years\' War</a> (1756&#8211;1763), control of Newfoundland once again became a major source of conflict between Britain, France and Spain who all pressed for a share in the valuable fishery there. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Britain_in_the_Seven_Years_War" title="Great Britain in the Seven Years War">Britain\'s victories around the globe</a> led <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt,_1st_Earl_of_Chatham" title="William Pitt, 1st Earl of Chatham">William Pitt</a> to insist that nobody other than Britain should have access to Newfoundland. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Signal_Hill" title="Battle of Signal Hill">Battle of Signal Hill</a> took place in Newfoundland in 1762 when a French force landed and tried to occupy the island, only to be repulsed by the British.\n</p><p>From 1763 to 1767 <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> made a detailed survey of the coasts of Newfoundland and southern Labrador while commander of  <a href="/wiki/HMS_Grenville_(1754)" title="HMS Grenville (1754)">HMS&#160;<i>Grenville</i></a>. (The following year, 1768, Cook began <a href="/wiki/First_voyage_of_James_Cook" title="First voyage of James Cook">his first circumnavigation of the world</a>.) In 1796 a Franco-Spanish expedition again <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_expedition" title="Newfoundland expedition">succeeded in raiding</a> the coasts of Newfoundland and Labrador, destroying many of the settlements.\n</p><p>By the Treaty of Utrecht (1713), French fishermen gained the right to land and cure fish on the "French Shore" on the western coast. (They had a permanent base on nearby <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Pierre_and_Miquelon" title="St. Pierre and Miquelon">St. Pierre and Miquelon</a> islands; the French gave up their French Shore rights in 1904.) In 1783 the British signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris</a> with the United States that gave American fishermen similar rights along the coast. These rights were reaffirmed by treaties in 1818, 1854 and 1871 and confirmed by arbitration in 1910.\n</p><p>In 1854 the British government established Newfoundland\'s <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">responsible government</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\nIn 1855, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Francis_Little" title="Philip Francis Little">Philip Francis Little</a>, a native of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a>, won a parliamentary majority over <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Hoyles" title="Hugh Hoyles">Hugh Hoyles</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_of_Newfoundland" title="Conservative Party of Newfoundland">Conservatives</a>. Little formed the first Newfoundland administration (1855-1858). Newfoundland rejected <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">confederation with Canada</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newfoundland_general_election,_1869" title="Newfoundland general election, 1869">1869 general election</a>. <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Minister of Canada</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Sparrow_David_Thompson" title="John Sparrow David Thompson">Sir John Thompson</a> came very close to negotiating Newfoundland\'s entry into Confederation in 1892.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominion_of_Newfoundland">Dominion of Newfoundland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Dominion of Newfoundland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Dominion of Newfoundland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dominion_of_Newfoundland_Red_Ensign.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Dominion_of_Newfoundland_Red_Ensign.svg/220px-Dominion_of_Newfoundland_Red_Ensign.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Dominion_of_Newfoundland_Red_Ensign.svg/330px-Dominion_of_Newfoundland_Red_Ensign.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Dominion_of_Newfoundland_Red_Ensign.svg/440px-Dominion_of_Newfoundland_Red_Ensign.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dominion_of_Newfoundland_Red_Ensign.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Newfoundland Red Ensign &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Civil_ensign" title="Civil ensign">civil ensign</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a> from 1904 to 1965.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THE_PROVINCES_Chap_XIX_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-THE_PROVINCES_Chap_XIX-66">[66]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Newfoundland remained a colony until acquiring Dominion status in 1907.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mapleweb_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-mapleweb-67">[67]</a></sup> A dominion constituted a self-governing state of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> or <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">British Commonwealth</a> and the Dominion of Newfoundland was relatively autonomous from British rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mapleweb_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-mapleweb-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">Union Flag</a> &#8211; official flag of the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Dominion of Newfoundland</a> from 1931 to 1949 and official flag of the province of Newfoundland until 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THE_PROVINCES_Chap_XIX_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-THE_PROVINCES_Chap_XIX-66">[66]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Newfoundland\'s own regiment, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Newfoundland_Regiment" title="Royal Newfoundland Regiment">1st Newfoundland Regiment</a>, fought in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a>. On July 1, 1916, nearly the entire regiment was wiped out at <a href="/wiki/Beaumont-Hamel_Newfoundland_Memorial" title="Beaumont-Hamel Newfoundland Memorial">Beaumont-Hamel</a> on the <a href="/wiki/First_day_on_the_Somme" title="First day on the Somme">first day on the Somme</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The regiment went on to serve with distinction in several subsequent battles, earning the prefix "Royal". Despite people\'s pride in the accomplishments of the regiment, the Dominion\'s war debt due to the regiment and the cost of maintaining a trans-island railway led to increased and ultimately unsustainable government debt in the post-war era.\n</p><p>Since the early 1800s, Newfoundland and Quebec (or Lower Canada) had been in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labrador_boundary_dispute" title="Labrador boundary dispute">border dispute</a> over the Labrador region. In 1927, however, the British government ruled that the area known as modern-day Labrador was to be considered part of the Dominion of Newfoundland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mapleweb_67-2"><a href="#cite_note-mapleweb-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commission_of_Government_and_confederation_with_Canada">Commission of Government and confederation with Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Commission of Government and confederation with Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Due to Newfoundland\'s high debt load arising from <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and construction of the <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_Railway" title="Newfoundland Railway">Newfoundland Railway</a>, and decreasing revenue due to the collapse of fish prices, the dominion legislature voted itself out of existence in 1933<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-collapse_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-collapse-69">[69]</a></sup> in exchange for loan guarantees by the Crown and a promise it would be re-established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malone_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Malone-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>8&#8211;10</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> On February 16, 1934, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commission_of_Government" title="Commission of Government">Commission of Government</a> was sworn in, ending 79 years of <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">responsible government</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-collapse_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-collapse-69">[69]</a></sup> The Commission consisted of seven persons appointed by the British government. For 15 years, no elections took place, and no legislature was convened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commission_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-commission-72">[72]</a></sup>\n</p><p>When prosperity returned with <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, agitation began to end the Commission and reinstate responsible government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Instead, the British government created the <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_National_Convention" title="Newfoundland National Convention">National Convention</a> in 1946, reflecting the efforts toward self-determination that arose in Europe following the war. The Convention, chaired by Judge <a href="/wiki/Cyril_J._Fox" title="Cyril J. Fox">Cyril J. Fox</a>, consisted of 45 elected members from across the dominion and was formally tasked with advising on the future of Newfoundland.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newfoundland_Second_Referendum_1948.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="325" decoding="async" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Newfoundland_Second_Referendum_1948.png/220px-Newfoundland_Second_Referendum_1948.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/Newfoundland_Second_Referendum_1948.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newfoundland_Second_Referendum_1948.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>How the electorate voted in the 1948 referendum</div></div></div>\n<p>Several motions were made by <a href="/wiki/Joey_Smallwood" title="Joey Smallwood">Joey Smallwood</a> (a convention member who later served as the first provincial premier of Newfoundland<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newtois_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-newtois-74">[74]</a></sup>) to examine joining Canada by sending a delegation to Ottawa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newtois_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-newtois-74">[74]</a></sup> The first motion was defeated, although the Convention later decided to send delegations to both London and Ottawa to explore alternatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> In January 1948, the National Convention voted against putting Confederation onto the referendum 29 to 16, but the British, which controlled the National Convention and the subsequent referendum, overruled this vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malone_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-Malone-70">[70]</a></sup> Those who supported Confederation were extremely disappointed with the recommendations of the National Convention and organized a petition, signed by more than 50,000 Newfoundlanders, demanding that confederation with Canada be placed before the people in the upcoming referendum. As most historians agree, the British government keenly wanted Confederation on the ballot and ensured that it would be.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Three main factions actively campaigned during the lead-up to the referenda. Smallwood led the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_Association" title="Confederate Association">Confederate Association</a> (CA), advocating entry into the Canadian Confederation. They campaigned through a newspaper known as <i>The Confederate</i>. The <a href="/wiki/Responsible_Government_League" title="Responsible Government League">Responsible Government League</a> (RGL), led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_Cashin" title="Peter Cashin">Peter Cashin</a>, advocated an independent Newfoundland with a return to responsible government. Their newspaper was <i>The Independent</i>. A third, the smaller <a href="/wiki/Economic_Union_Party" title="Economic Union Party">Economic Union Party</a> (EUP), led by <a href="/wiki/Chesley_Crosbie" title="Chesley Crosbie">Chesley Crosbie</a>, advocated closer economic ties with the United States. Though a 1947 poll found 80% of Newfoundland residents wanting to become Americans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> the EUP failed to gain much attention and merged with the RGL after the first referendum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factions_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-factions-79">[79]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first referendum took place on June 3, 1948; 44.6% of people voted for responsible government, 41.1% voted for confederation with Canada, while 14.3% voted for the Commission of Government. Since none of the choices had gained over 50%, a second referendum with only the two more popular choices was held on July 22, 1948. The official outcome of that referendum was 52.3% for confederation with Canada and 47.7% for responsible (independent) government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-historyquatre_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-historyquatre-80">[80]</a></sup> After the referendum, the British governor named a seven-man delegation to negotiate Canada\'s offer on behalf of Newfoundland. After six of the delegation signed, the British government passed the <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_Act" title="Newfoundland Act">British North America Act, 1949</a> through <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament</a>. Newfoundland officially joined Canada at midnight on March 31, 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-historyquatre_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-historyquatre-80">[80]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As documents in British and Canadian archives became available in the 1980s, it became clear that both Canada and the United Kingdom wanted Newfoundland to join Canada. Some have charged that it was a conspiracy to manoeuvre Newfoundland into Confederation in exchange for forgiveness of Britain\'s war debt and for other considerations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malone_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-Malone-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>68</span></sup> Yet, most historians who have examined the government documents have concluded that, while Britain engineered the inclusion of a Confederation option in the referendum, Newfoundlanders made the final decision themselves, if by a narrow margin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the referendum, there was a rumour that the referendum had been narrowly won by the "responsible government" side, but that the result had been fixed by the <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Macdonald,_1st_Baron_Macdonald_of_Gwaenysgor" title="Gordon Macdonald, 1st Baron Macdonald of Gwaenysgor">British governor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malone_70-3"><a href="#cite_note-Malone-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>225&#8211;26</span></sup> Shortly after the referendum, several boxes of ballots from St. John\'s were burned by order of <a href="/wiki/Herman_William_Quinton" title="Herman William Quinton">Herman William Quinton</a>, one of only two commissioners who supported confederation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malone_70-4"><a href="#cite_note-Malone-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>224</span></sup> Some have argued that independent oversight of the vote tallying was lacking, though the process was supervised by respected Corner Brook Magistrate Nehemiah Short, who had also overseen elections to the National Convention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malone_70-5"><a href="#cite_note-Malone-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>224&#8211;25</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Provincial_flag">Provincial flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Provincial flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador.svg/220px-Flag_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador.svg/330px-Flag_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador.svg/440px-Flag_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Flag of Newfoundland and Labrador">Flag of Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, adopted as the provincial flag on May 28, 1980</div></div></div>\n<p>Newfoundland and Labrador\'s present <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Flag of Newfoundland and Labrador">provincial flag</a>, designed by Newfoundland artist <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Pratt" title="Christopher Pratt">Christopher Pratt</a>, was officially adopted by the legislature on May 28, 1980, and first flown on "Discovery Day" that year. Labrador has its own <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Labrador" title="Flag of Labrador">unofficial flag</a>, created in 1973 by Mike Martin, former <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Legislative_Assembly" title="Member of the Legislative Assembly">Member of the Legislative Assembly</a> for Labrador South.\n</p><p>The blue is meant to represent the sea, the white represents snow and ice, the red represents the efforts and struggles of the people, and the gold represents the confidence of Newfoundlanders and Labradorians. The blue triangles are a tribute to the Union Flag, and represent the British heritage of the province. The two red triangles represent Labrador (the mainland portion of the province) and the island. In Pratt\'s words, the golden arrow points towards a "brighter future".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Newfoundland_Flag_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Newfoundland_Flag-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newfoundland_Tricolour.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Newfoundland_Tricolour.svg/220px-Newfoundland_Tricolour.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Newfoundland_Tricolour.svg/330px-Newfoundland_Tricolour.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Newfoundland_Tricolour.svg/440px-Newfoundland_Tricolour.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newfoundland_Tricolour.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Newfoundland tri-colour flag &#8211; unofficial (1870s or later)</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_Tricolour" title="Newfoundland Tricolour">"Pink, White and Green"</a> is a flag of 19th-century origins that enjoyed popularity in portions of the island in the late 19th century. It was flown on some vessels into the 20th century. It was never adopted by the Newfoundland government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THE_PROVINCES_Chap_XIX_66-2"><a href="#cite_note-THE_PROVINCES_Chap_XIX-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A 1976 article reported that the tricolour flag was created in 1843 by then Roman Catholic Bishop of Newfoundland, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Anthony_Fleming" title="Michael Anthony Fleming">Michael Anthony Fleming</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-monitor_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-monitor-83">[83]</a></sup> The colours were intended to represent the symbolic union of Newfoundland\'s historically dominant ethnic/religious groups: English, Scots and Irish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-monitor_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-monitor-83">[83]</a></sup> Though popular, there is no historical evidence to support this legend.\n</p><p>Recent scholarship  suggests that the flag was first used in the 1870s or later by the Roman Catholic "Star of the Sea" fishermen\'s association. It resembled the unofficial <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Ireland" title="Flag of Ireland">flag of Ireland</a>. The tri-colour flag remained relatively unknown outside of St. John\'s and the Avalon peninsula until the growth of the tourist industry since the late 20th century. It has been used as an emblem on items in gift shops in St. John\'s and other towns. Some tourists assume it is the Irish flag.\n</p><p>The "Pink, White and Green" has been adopted by some residents as a symbol of ties with Irish heritage and as a political statement. Many of the province\'s <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a>, who make up nearly 60% of the province\'s total population,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Population_by_religion,_by_province_and_territory_(2001_Census)_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Population_by_religion,_by_province_and_territory_(2001_Census)-84">[84]</a></sup> may not identify with this heritage.\n</p><p>At the same time, many of the province\'s Catholics, approximately 37% of the total population (with at least 22% of the population claiming Irish ancestry),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-renamed_from_2006_on_20151223002828_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-renamed_from_2006_on_20151223002828-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Religions_in_Canada:_Newfoundland_and_Labrador_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Religions_in_Canada:_Newfoundland_and_Labrador-86">[86]</a></sup> think that the current provincial flag does not satisfactorily represent them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Emblem_of_our_country_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Emblem_of_our_country-87">[87]</a></sup> But, a government-sponsored poll in 2005 revealed that 75% of Newfoundlanders rejected adoption of the Tricolour flag as the province\'s official flag.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-poll_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-poll-88">[88]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-confederation_and_current_provincial_anthem">Pre-confederation and current provincial anthem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Pre-confederation and current provincial anthem">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ode_to_Newfoundland" title="Ode to Newfoundland">Ode to Newfoundland</a></div>\n<p>The pre-confederation and current provincial anthem is the "<a href="/wiki/Ode_to_Newfoundland" title="Ode to Newfoundland">Ode to Newfoundland</a>", written by British colonial governor Sir <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Cavendish_Boyle" title="Charles Cavendish Boyle">Charles Cavendish Boyle</a> in 1902 during his administration of Newfoundland (1901 to 1904). It was adopted as the official Newfoundland anthem on May 20, 1904. In 1980, the province re-adopted the song as an official provincial anthem, making this the only province in Canada to officially adopt an anthem. "The Ode to Newfoundland" is still sung at public events in Newfoundland and Labrador.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newfoundland_and_Labrador&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greenspond_Newfoundland_Canada.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2538" data-file-width="3791" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Greenspond_Newfoundland_Canada.jpg/220px-Greenspond_Newfoundland_Canada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Greenspond_Newfoundland_Canada.jpg/330px-Greenspond_Newfoundland_Canada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Greenspond_Newfoundland_Canada.jpg/440px-Greenspond_Newfoundland_Canada.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greenspond_Newfoundland_Canada.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Greenspond" title="Greenspond">Greenspond</a> on the northeast coast of Newfoundland</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Demographics of Newfoundland and Labrador">Demographics of Newfoundland and Labrador</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_communities_in_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="List of communities in Newfoundland and Labrador">List of communities in Newfoundland and Labrador</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador_communities_by_population" title="List of Newfoundland and Labrador communities by population">List of Newfoundland and Labrador communities by population</a></div>\n<p>Newfoundland and Labrador has a population of 519,716,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016census_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-2016census-2">[2]</a></sup> more than half of whom live on the <a href="/wiki/Avalon_Peninsula" title="Avalon Peninsula">Avalon Peninsula</a> of Newfoundland, site of the capital and historical early settlement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Since 2006, the population of the province has started to increase for the first time since the early 1990s. In the 2006 census the population of the province decreased by 1.5% compared to 2001, and stood at 505,469.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> But, by the 2011 census, the population had risen by 1.8%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011census_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-2011census-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 33.33%;text-align: left; vertical-align: Newfoundland and Labrador">St. John\'s</a>\n</td>\n<td>100,646\n</td>\n<td>106,172\n</td>\n<td>108,860\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Conception_Bay_South" title="Conception Bay South">Conception Bay South</a>\n</td>\n<td>21,966\n</td>\n<td>24,848\n</td>\n<td>26,199\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Mount_Pearl" title="Mount Pearl">Mount Canada</a></i>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="width: 33.33%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<p><b>Languages of the population (2011)</b>\n</p>\n<table language">Arabic</a>\n</td>\n<td>540\n</td>\n<td>0.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>10.\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>\n</td>\n<td>300\n</td>\n<td>&lt;
